<text>After moving to LA recently I spent a lot of time reading reviews on Google trying to find a new barber. Every listing has reviews claiming that they give the best haircut in LA side by side with others talking about the disastrous cut they received. But I can honestly say that my experience at Vinny‚Äôs was nothing short of perfect.

I made an appointment with Omar using the very easy to use (even on mobile) website. As mentioned in other reviews parking is indeed hard to come by, but it only took me about five minutes to find a spot that was just a few minutes walk away. There are two front doors to the place, but the one to the left has a small but comfortable waiting room. I was delighted to find a truly old school barber shop, with smartly dressed men in white smocks and shiny shoes giving all kinds of guys all kinds of haircuts.

Though I was early I didn‚Äôt have to wait long for Omar to greet me warmly and ask what I wanted. I‚Äôll admit, my descriptions were vague as I was used to seeing my regular barber and never having to describe what exactly I wanted. But he listened intently before getting to work quickly, and soon the floor around us was covered in hair. It was a hot day and I have some social anxiety, so I was sweating a little more than I would have liked, which I know can make giving a close fade a real challenge. But Omar was great, stopping every so often to dry my hair and face.

When I put on my glasses and he held up a mirror to show me his work I was amazed at how good everything looked. He gave me exactly what I wanted, perfectly shaping my hair and beard to highlight my best features. The cost was very reasonable for the quality of work received, but keep in mind it is a cash only place. I will definitely be back for my next cut, happy to have finally found a great barber In my area. Thanks Omar!<//text><UserId.>112969645770324727761<//UserId.>< Date>

<rating>2< /rating>< text>
Beware if you are thinking of going here for brunch with four or more people!

I have been many times to Oscar's as a party of two, and have liked it.

But, today I had a reservation for four people, and they stuck us at a two top. When I asked to be seated at a four top, the host told me that they do not do that anymore. All parties of four have to squeeze into a table for two so they can fill the restaurant to the gills...even when the two top next to us opened up. What did they do? They told us no, and sat another party of four at the two top next to us. Everyone in both parties were uncomfortable.

When our food came there wasn't enough room on the small table to hold all four plates. It was completely unacceptable, and the host did not care less.

They screwed up our food order, and two of the four had to wait for the kitchen to remake our meals while the other two people's food got cold.

It's too bad because I used to like this place. But, today will be the last time. The two people who had to sit on the stools on the passageway were continually bumped into throughout the meal.

For a brunch costing $100,  we should not have to have been told "sorry" a total of seven times when we told them about the food mix-up, the fact that we were feeling way too cramped and when we waited forever to have them pick up our credit card and run it so we could get out of there.

Sorry never felt so insincere.<//text>

< text>
Looks like a hip place, but apparently, my wife and I and two teenage daughters were not hip enough. When we arrived at 7:45 PM, famished and looking forward to a good meal, the the pretty young brunette hostess proceeded to look past and through us and receive two younger patrons ahead of us. She did not even acknowledge our presence or ever speak to us, even though I was standing directly in front of her. Finally, her (somewhat) older counterpart came forward and put us on the waiting list, claiming that it would be a two hour wait for a party of four. This seemed hugely exaggerated given the level of business and what we overheard being told to the people taken before us. It turned out to be true as we were texted in a little over an hour that our table was ready, an hour less than the rudely delivered estimate of two hour wait. Luckily for us, we had already eaten at another nearby restaurant - The Firehouse - where we were greeted warmly and enjoyed a great meal with great service.< /text>

<name>Bryan Hall<//name><UserId.>114871459955171185614< /UserId.><Resp>None</Resp><pictures>None<//pictures><text>I've passed these courts for years but just played there for the first time this weekend. There are 5 courts here that are free and open to the public. They are first come first served. One strange thing about this small park is there is no parking lot at all, just street parking.

The courts themselves are decent. Some of the corners could use some cleaning, due to trash left behind by others. There seems to be a few homeless people/loiterers nearby but not threatening at all. A cool feature of these courts is the view of the DTLA skyline. If you don't like noise, the 101 freeway traffic may be a disturbance, but I was able to block it out. I would definitely play here again.</text></record>

The Laguna Niguel Farmers Market has a very good blend of farm grown produce and fruit as well as healthy alternative products. You can buy fresh bread there, grass-fed beef and even fish. <Time>1520969326406<//Time><rating>5</rating>< review>
Great little market.

Plenty of parking and it's not too busy, so you can usually get what you need easily.

There is an awesome selection of vendors too:

Coffee, fruits, vegetables, nuts, yogurts, breads, juices, essential oils, pastries, tamales, soups, seasonings, flowers, succulents, eggs, kombucha, everything!

Starts at 8 am and shuts down at noon, so it is a great way to kick off your Sunday.</review>
